See below for how to use a specific Scala version or all of the supported Scala versions.\\n17: \\n18: ### Build a jar and run it ###\\n19:     ./gradlew jar\\n20: \\n21: Follow instructions in https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\\n22: \\n23: ### Build source jar ###\\n24:     ./gradlew srcJar\\n25: \\n26: ### Build aggregated javadoc ###\\n27:     ./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\\n28: \\n29: ### Build javadoc and scaladoc ###\\n30:     ./gradlew javadoc\\n31:     ./gradlew javadocJar # builds a javadoc jar for each module\\n32:     ./gradlew scaladoc\\n33:     ./gradlew scaladocJar # builds a scaladoc jar for each module\\n34:     ./gradlew docsJar # builds both (if applicable) javadoc and scaladoc jars for each module\\n35: \\n36: ### Run unit/integration tests ###\\n37:     ./gradlew test # runs both unit and integration tests\\n38:     ./gradlew unitTest\\n39:     ./gradlew integrationTest\\n40:     \\n41: ### Force re-running tests without code change ###\\n42:     ./gradlew test --rerun\\n43:     ./gradlew unitTest --rerun\\n44:     ./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\\n45: \\n46: ### Running a particular unit/integration test ###\\n47:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\\n48: \\n49: ### Repeatedly running a particular unit/integration test ###\\n50:     I=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \\\"Completed run: $I\\\"; sleep 1; done\\n51: \\n52: ### Running a particular test method within a unit/integration test ###\\n53:     ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\\n54:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\\n55: \\n56: ### Running a particular unit/integration test with log4j output ###\\n57: By default, there will be only small number of logs output while testing. You can adjust it by changing the `log4j.properties` file in the module's `src/test/resources` directory.\\n58: \\n59: For example, if you want to see more logs for clients project tests, you can modify [the line](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties#L21) in `clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties` \\n60: to `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO` and then run:\\n61:     \\n62:     ./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest   \\n63: \\n64: And you should see `INFO` level logs in the file under the `clients/build/test-results/test` directory.\\n65: \\n66: ### Specifying test retries ###\\n67: By default, each failed test is retried once up to a maximum of five retries per test run. Tests are retried at the end of the test task. Adjust these parameters in the following way:\\n68: \\n69:     ./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\\n70:     \\n71: See [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\\n72: \\n73: ### Generating test coverage reports ###\\n74: Generate coverage reports for the whole project:\\n75: \\n76:     ./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\\n77: \\n78: Generate coverage for a single module, i.e.: \\n79: \\n80:     ./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\\n81:     \\n82: ### Building a binary release gzipped tar ball ###\\n83:     ./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\\n84: \\n85: The release file can be found inside `./core/build/distributions/`.\\n86: \\n87: ### Building auto generated messages ###\\n88: Sometimes it is only necessary to rebuild the RPC auto-generated message data when switching between branches, as they could\\n89: fail due to code changes. You can just run:\\n90:  \\n91:     ./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\\n92: \\n93: ### Running a Kafka broker in KRaft mode\\n94: \\n95: Using compiled files:\\n96: \\n97:     KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID=\\\"$(./bin/kafka-storage.sh random-uuid)\\\"\\n98:     ./bin/kafka-storage.sh format -t $KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID -c config/kraft/server.properties\\n99:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/kraft/server.properties\\n100: \\n101: Using docker image:\\n102: \\n103:     docker run -p 9092:9092 apache/kafka:3.7.0\\n104: \\n105: ### Running a Kafka broker in ZooKeeper mode\\n106: \\n107: Using compiled files:\\n108: \\n109:     ./bin/zookeeper-server-start.sh config/zookeeper.properties\\n110:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/server.properties\\n111: \\n112: >Since ZooKeeper mode is already deprecated and planned to be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0, the docker image only supports running in KRaft mode\\n113: \\n114: ### Cleaning the build ###\\n115:     ./gradlew clean\\n116: \\n117: ### Running a task with one of the Scala versions available (2.12.x or 2.13.x) ###\\n118: *Note that if building the jars with a version other than 2.13.x, you need to set the `SCALA_VERSION` variable or change it in `bin/kafka-run-class.sh` to run the quick start.*\\n119: \\n120: You can pass either the major version (eg 2.12) or the full version (eg 2.12.7):\\n121: \\n122:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\\n123:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 test\\n124:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 releaseTarGz\\n125: \\n126: ### Running a task with all the scala versions enabled by default ###\\n127: \\n128: Invoke the `gradlewAll` script followed by the task(s):\\n129: \\n130:     ./gradlewAll test\\n131:     ./gradlewAll jar\\n132:     ./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\\n133: \\n134: ### Running a task for a specific project ###\\n135: This is for `core`, `examples` and `clients`\\n136: \\n137:     ./gradlew core:jar\\n138:     ./gradlew core:test\\n139: \\n140: Streams has multiple sub-projects, but you can run all the tests:\\n141: \\n142:     ./gradlew :streams:testAll\\n143: \\n144: ### Listing all gradle tasks ###\\n145:     ./gradlew tasks\\n146: \\n147: ### Building IDE project ####\\n148: *Note that this is not strictly necessary (IntelliJ IDEA has good built-in support for Gradle projects, for example).*\\n149: \\n150:     ./gradlew eclipse\\n151:     ./gradlew idea\\n152: \\n153: The `eclipse` task has been configured to use `${project_dir}/build_eclipse` as Eclipse's build directory. Eclipse's default\\n154: build directory (`${project_dir}/bin`) clashes with Kafka's scripts directory and we don't use Gradle's build directory\\n155: to avoid known issues with this configuration.\\n156: \\n157: ### Publishing the jar for all versions of Scala and for all projects to maven ###\\n158: The recommended command is:\\n159: \\n160:     ./gradlewAll publish\\n161: \\n162: For backwards compatibility, the following also works:\\n163: \\n164:     ./gradlewAll uploadArchives\\n165: \\n166: Please note for this to work you should create/update `${GRADLE_USER_HOME}/gradle.properties` (typically, `~/.gradle/gradle.properties`) and assign the following variables\\n167: \\n168:     mavenUrl=\\n169:     mavenUsername=\\n170:     mavenPassword=\\n171:     signing.keyId=\\n172:     signing.password=\\n173:     signing.secretKeyRingFile=\\n174: \\n175: ### Publishing the streams quickstart archetype artifact to maven ###\\n176: For the Streams archetype project, one cannot use gradle to upload to maven; instead the `mvn deploy` command needs to be called at the quickstart folder:\\n177: \\n178:     cd streams/quickstart\\n179:     mvn deploy\\n180: \\n181: Please note for this to work you should create/update user maven settings (typically, `${USER_HOME}/.m2/settings.xml`) to assign the following variables\\n182: \\n183:     <settings xmlns=\\\"http://maven.apache.org/SETTINGS/1.0.0\\\"\\n184:        xmlns:xsi=\\\"http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance\\\"\\n185:        xsi:schemaLocation=\\\"http://maven.apache.org/SETTINGS/1.0.0\\n186:                            https://maven.apache.org/xsd/settings-1.0.0.xsd\\\">\\n187:     ...                           \\n188: <password>${maven_password}</password>\\n194:        </server>\\n195:        <server>\\n196:           <id>apache.releases.https</id>\\n197:           <username>${maven_username}</username>\\n198:           <password>${maven_password}</password>\\n199:         </server>\\n200:         ...\\n201:      </servers>\\n202:      ...\\n203: \\n204: \\n205: ### Installing ALL the jars to the local Maven repository ###\\n206: The recommended command to build for both Scala 2.12 and 2.13 is:\\n207: \\n208:     ./gradlewAll publishToMavenLocal\\n209: \\n210: For backwards compatibility, the following testJar\\n222: \\n223: ### Running code quality checks ###\\n224: There are two code quality analysis tools that we regularly run, spotbugs and checkstyle.\\n225: \\n226: #### Checkstyle ####\\n227: Checkstyle enforces a consistent coding style in Kafka.\\n228: You can run checkstyle using:\\n229: \\n230:     ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\\n231: \\n232: The checkstyle warnings will be found in `reports/checkstyle/reports/main.html` and `reports/checkstyle/reports/test.html` files in the\\n233: subproject build directories. They are also printed to the console. The build will fail if Checkstyle fails.\\n234: \\n235: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessCheck` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\\n236: \\n237: #### Spotless ####\\n238: The import order is a part of static check. please call `spotlessApply` (require JDK 11+) to optimize the imports of Java codes before filing pull request.\\n239: \\n240:     ./gradlew spotlessApply\\n241: \\n242: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessApply` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\\n243: \\n244: #### Spotbugs ####\\n245: Spotbugs uses static analysis to look for bugs in the code.\\n246: You can run spotbugs using:\\n247: \\n248:     ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\\n249: \\n250: The spotbugs warnings will be found in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `reports/spotbugs/test.html` files in the subproject build\\n251: directories.  Use -PxmlSpotBugsReport=true to generate an XML report instead of an HTML one.\\n252: \\n253: ### JMH microbenchmarks ###\\n254: We use [JMH](https://openjdk.java.net/projects/code-tools/jmh/) to write microbenchmarks that produce reliable results in the JVM.\\n255:     \\n256: See [jmh-benchmarks/README.md](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/jmh-benchmarks/README.md) for details on how to run the microbenchmarks.\\n257: \\n258: ### Dependency Analysis ###\\n259: \\n260: The gradle [dependency debugging documentation](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/viewing_debugging_dependencies.html) mentions using the `dependencies` or `dependencyInsight` tasks to debug dependencies for the root project or individual subprojects.\\n261: \\n262: Alternatively, use the `allDeps` or `allDepInsight` tasks for recursively iterating through all subprojects:\\n263: \\n264:     ./gradlew allDeps\\n265: \\n266:     ./gradlew allDepInsight --configuration runtimeClasspath --dependency com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind\\n267: \\n268: These take the same arguments as the builtin variants.\\n269: \\n270: ### Determining if any dependencies could be updated ###\\n271:     ./gradlew dependencyUpdates\\n272: \\n273: ### Common build options ###\\n274: \\n275: The following options should be set with a `-P` switch, for example `./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=1 test`.\\n276: \\n277: * `commitId`: sets the build commit ID as .git/HEAD might not be correct if there are local commits added for build purposes.\\n278: * `mavenUrl`: sets the URL of the maven deployment repository (`file://path/to/repo` can be used to point to a local repository).\\n279: * `maxParallelForks`: maximum number of test processes to start in parallel. Defaults to the number of processors available to the JVM.\\n280: * `maxScalacThreads`: maximum number of worker threads for the scalac backend. Defaults to the lowest of `8` and the number of processors\\n281: available to the JVM. The value must be between 1 and 16 (inclusive). \\n282: * `ignoreFailures`: ignore test failures from junit\\n283: * `showStandardStreams`: shows standard out and standard error of the test JVM(s) on the console.\\n284: * `skipSigning`: skips signing of artifacts.\\n285: * `testLoggingEvents`: unit test events to be logged, separated by comma. For example `./gradlew -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed test`.\\n286: * `xmlSpotBugsReport`: enable XML reports for spotBugs. This also disables HTML reports as only one can be enabled at a time.\\n287: * `maxTestRetries`: maximum number of retries for a failing test case.\\n288: * `maxTestRetryFailures`: maximum number of test failures before retrying is disabled for subsequent tests.\\n289: * `enableTestCoverage`: enables test coverage plugins and tasks, including bytecode enhancement of classes required to track said\\n290: coverage. Note that this introduces some overhead when running tests and hence why it's disabled by default (the overhead\\n291: varies, but 15-20% is a reasonable estimate).\\n292: * `keepAliveMode`: configures the keep alive mode for the Gradle compilation daemon - reuse improves start-up time. The values should \\n293: be one of `daemon` or `session` (the default is `daemon`). `daemon` keeps the daemon alive until it's explicitly stopped while\\n294: `session` keeps it alive until the end of the build session. This currently only affects the Scala compiler, see\\n295: https://github.com/gradle/gradle/pull/21034 for a PR that attempts to do the same for the Java compiler.\\n296: * `scalaOptimizerMode`: configures the optimizing behavior of the scala compiler, the value should be one of `none`, `method`, `inline-kafka` or\\n297: `inline-scala` (the default is `inline-kafka`). `none` is the scala compiler default, which only eliminates unreachable code. `method` also\\n298: includes method-local optimizations. `inline-kafka` adds inlining of methods within the kafka packages. Finally, `inline-scala` also\\n299: includes inlining of methods within the scala library (which avoids lambda allocations for methods like `Option.exists`). `inline-scala` is\\n300: only safe if the Scala library version is the same at compile time and runtime. Since we cannot guarantee this for all cases (for example, users\\n301: may depend on the kafka jar for integration tests where they may include a scala library with a different version), we don't enable it by\\n302: default. See https://www.lightbend.com/blog/scala-inliner-optimizer for more details.\\n303: \\n304: ### Running system tests ###\\n305: \\n306: See [tests/README.md](tests/README.md).\\n307: \\n308: ### Running in Vagrant ###\\n309: \\n310: See [vagrant/README.md](vagrant/README.md).\\n311: \\n312: ### Contribution ###\\n313: \\n314: Apache Kafka is interested in building the community; we would welcome any thoughts or [patches](https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA). repository ###\\n206: The recommended command to build for both Scala 2.12 and 2.13 is:\\n207: \\n208:     ./gradlewAll publishToMavenLocal\\n209: \\n210: For backwards compatibility, the following testJar\\n222: \\n223: ### Running code quality checks ###\\n224: There are two code quality analysis tools that we regularly run, spotbugs and checkstyle.\\n225: \\n226: #### Checkstyle ####\\n227: Checkstyle enforces a consistent coding style in Kafka.\\n228: You can run checkstyle using:\\n229: \\n230:     ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\\n231: \\n232: The checkstyle warnings will be found in `reports/checkstyle/reports/main.html` and `reports/checkstyle/reports/test.html` files in the\\n233: subproject build directories. They are also printed to the console. The build will fail if Checkstyle fails.\\n234: \\n235: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessCheck` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\\n236: \\n237: #### Spotless ####\\n238: The import order is a part of static check. please call `spotlessApply` (require JDK 11+) to optimize the imports of Java codes before filing pull request.\\n239: \\n240:     ./gradlew spotlessApply\\n241: \\n242: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessApply` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\\n243: \\n244: #### Spotbugs ####\\n245: Spotbugs uses static analysis to look for bugs in the code.\\n246: You can run spotbugs using:\\n247: \\n248:     ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\\n249: \\n250: The spotbugs warnings will be found in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `reports/spotbugs/test.html` files in the subproject build\\n251: directories.  Use -PxmlSpotBugsReport=true to generate an XML report instead of an HTML one.\\n252: \\n253: ### JMH microbenchmarks ###\\n254: We use [JMH](https://openjdk.java.net/projects/code-tools/jmh/) to write microbenchmarks that produce reliable results in the JVM.\\n255:     \\n256: See [jmh-benchmarks/README.md](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/jmh-benchmarks/README.md) for details on how to run the microbenchmarks.\\n257: \\n258: ### Dependency Analysis ###\\n259: \\n260: The gradle [dependency debugging documentation](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/viewing_debugging_dependencies.html) mentions using the `dependencies` or `dependencyInsight` tasks to debug dependencies for the root project or individual subprojects.\\n261: \\n262: Alternatively, use the `allDeps` or `allDepInsight` tasks for recursively iterating through all subprojects:\\n263: \\n264:     ./gradlew allDeps\\n265: \\n266:     ./gradlew allDepInsight --configuration runtimeClasspath --dependency com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind\\n267: \\n268: These take the same arguments as the builtin variants.\\n269: \\n270: ### Determining if any dependencies could be updated ###\\n271:     ./gradlew dependencyUpdates\\n272: \\n273: ### Common build options ###\\n274: \\n275: The following options should be set with a `-P` switch, for example `./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=1 test`.\\n276: \\n277: * `commitId`: sets the build commit ID as .git/HEAD might not be correct if there are local commits added for build purposes.\\n278: * `mavenUrl`: sets the URL of the maven deployment repository (`file://path/to/repo` can be used to point to a local repository).\\n279: * `maxParallelForks`: maximum number of test processes to start in parallel. Defaults to the number of processors available to the JVM.\\n280: * `maxScalacThreads`: maximum number of worker threads for the scalac backend. Defaults to the lowest of `8` and the number of processors\\n281: available to the JVM. The value must be between 1 and 16 (inclusive). \\n282: * `ignoreFailures`: ignore test failures from junit\\n283: * `showStandardStreams`: shows standard out and standard error of the test JVM(s) on the console.\\n284: * `skipSigning`: skips signing of artifacts.\\n285: * `testLoggingEvents`: unit test events to be logged, separated by comma. For example `./gradlew -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed test`.\\n286: * `xmlSpotBugsReport`: enable XML reports for spotBugs. This also disables HTML reports as only one can be enabled at a time.\\n287: * `maxTestRetries`: maximum number of retries for a failing test case.\\n288: * `maxTestRetryFailures`: maximum number of test failures before retrying is disabled for subsequent tests.\\n289: * `enableTestCoverage`: enables test coverage plugins and tasks, including bytecode enhancement of classes required to track said\\n290: coverage. Note that this introduces some overhead when running tests and hence why it's disabled by default (the overhead\\n291: varies, but 15-20% is a reasonable estimate).\\n292: * `keepAliveMode`: configures the keep alive mode for the Gradle compilation daemon - reuse improves start-up time. The values should \\n293: be one of `daemon` or `session` (the default is `daemon`). `daemon` keeps the daemon alive until it's explicitly stopped while\\n294: `session` keeps it alive until the end of the build session. This currently only affects the Scala compiler, see\\n295: https://github.com/gradle/gradle/pull/21034 for a PR that attempts to do the same for the Java compiler.\\n296: * `scalaOptimizerMode`: configures the optimizing behavior of the scala compiler, the value should be one of `none`, `method`, `inline-kafka` or\\n297: `inline-scala` (the default is `inline-kafka`). `none` is the scala compiler default, which only eliminates unreachable code. `method` also\\n298: includes method-local optimizations. `inline-kafka` adds inlining of methods within the kafka packages. Finally, `inline-scala` also\\n299: includes inlining of methods within the scala library (which avoids lambda allocations for methods like `Option.exists`). `inline-scala` is\\n300: only safe if the Scala library version is the same at compile time and runtime. Since we cannot guarantee this for all cases (for example, users\\n301: may depend on the kafka jar for integration tests where they may include a scala library with a different version), we don't enable it by\\n302: default. See https://www.lightbend.com/blog/scala-inliner-optimizer for more details.\\n303: \\n304: ### Running system tests ###\\n305: \\n306: See [tests/README.md](tests/README.md).\\n307: \\n308: ### Running in Vagrant ###\\n309: \\n310: See [vagrant/README.md](vagrant/README.md).\\n311: \\n312: ### Contribution ###\\n313: \\n314: Apache Kafka is interested in building the community; we would welcome any thoughts or [patches](https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA). You can reach us [on the Apache mailing lists](http://kafka.apache.org/contact.html).\\n315: \\n316: To contribute follow the instructions here:\\n317:  * https://kafka.apache.org/contributing.html \\n318: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--3.9.0@5010d340da347c7e58d0b503d83a5a892a29c127/-/blob/README.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: Apache Kafka\n2: =================\n3: See our [web site](https://kafka.apache.org) for details on the project.\n4: \n5: You need to have [Java](http://www.oracle.com/technetwork/java/javase/downloads/index.html) installed.\n6: \n7: We build and test Apache Kafka with Java 8, 11, 17 and 21. We set the `release` parameter in javac and scalac\n8: to `8` to ensure the generated binaries are compatible with Java 8 or higher (independently of the Java version\n9: used for compilation). Java 8 support project-wide has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.0, Java 11 support for\n10: the broker and tools has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.7 and removal of both is planned for Apache Kafka 4.0 (\n11: see [KIP-750](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308223) and\n12: [KIP-1013](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=284789510) for more details).\n13: \n14: Scala 2.12 and 2.13 are supported and 2.13 is used by default. Scala 2.12 support has been deprecated since\n15: Apache Kafka 3.0 and will be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0 (see [KIP-751](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308218)\n16: for more details). See below for how to use a specific Scala version or all of the supported Scala versions.\n17: \n18: ### Build a jar and run it ###\n19:     ./gradlew jar\n20: \n21: Follow instructions in https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\n22: \n23: ### Build source jar ###\n24:     ./gradlew srcJar\n25: \n26: ### Build aggregated javadoc ###\n27:     ./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\n28: \n29: ### Build javadoc and scaladoc ###\n30:     ./gradlew javadoc\n31:     ./gradlew javadocJar # builds a javadoc jar for each module\n32:     ./gradlew scaladoc\n33:     ./gradlew scaladocJar # builds a scaladoc jar for each module\n34:     ./gradlew docsJar # builds both (if applicable) javadoc and scaladoc jars for each module\n35: \n36: ### Run unit/integration tests ###\n37:     ./gradlew test # runs both unit and integration tests\n38:     ./gradlew unitTest\n39:     ./gradlew integrationTest\n40:     \n41: ### Force re-running tests without code change ###\n42:     ./gradlew test --rerun\n43:     ./gradlew unitTest --rerun\n44:     ./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\n45: \n46: ### Running a particular unit/integration test ###\n47:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\n48: \n49: ### Repeatedly running a particular unit/integration test ###\n50:     I=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \"Completed run: $I\"; sleep 1; done\n51: \n52: ### Running a particular test method within a unit/integration test ###\n53:     ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\n54:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\n55: \n56: ### Running a particular unit/integration test with log4j output ###\n57: By default, there will be only small number of logs output while testing. You can adjust it by changing the `log4j.properties` file in the module's `src/test/resources` directory.\n58: \n59: For example, if you want to see more logs for clients project tests, you can modify [the line](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties#L21) in `clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties` \n60: to `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO` and then run:\n61:     \n62:     ./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest   \n63: \n64: And you should see `INFO` level logs in the file under the `clients/build/test-results/test` directory.\n65: \n66: ### Specifying test retries ###\n67: By default, each failed test is retried once up to a maximum of five retries per test run. Tests are retried at the end of the test task. Adjust these parameters in the following way:\n68: \n69:     ./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\n70:     \n71: See [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\n72: \n73: ### Generating test coverage reports ###\n74: Generate coverage reports for the whole project:\n75: \n76:     ./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n77: \n78: Generate coverage for a single module, i.e.: \n79: \n80:     ./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n81:     \n82: ### Building a binary release gzipped tar ball ###\n83:     ./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\n84: \n85: The release file can be found inside `./core/build/distributions/`.\n86: \n87: ### Building auto generated messages ###\n88: Sometimes it is only necessary to rebuild the RPC auto-generated message data when switching between branches, as they could\n89: fail due to code changes. You can just run:\n90:  \n91:     ./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\n92: \n93: ### Running a Kafka broker in KRaft mode\n94: \n95: Using compiled files:\n96: \n97:     KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID=\"$(./bin/kafka-storage.sh random-uuid)\"\n98:     ./bin/kafka-storage.sh format -t $KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID -c config/kraft/server.properties\n99:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/kraft/server.properties\n100: \n101: Using docker image:\n102: \n103:     docker run -p 9092:9092 apache/kafka:3.7.0\n104: \n105: ### Running a Kafka broker in ZooKeeper mode\n106: \n107: Using compiled files:\n108: \n109:     ./bin/zookeeper-server-start.sh config/zookeeper.properties\n110:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/server.properties\n111: \n112: >Since ZooKeeper mode is already deprecated and planned to be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0, the docker image only supports running in KRaft mode\n113: \n114: ### Cleaning the build ###\n115:     ./gradlew clean\n116: \n117: ### Running a task with one of the Scala versions available (2.12.x or 2.13.x) ###\n118: *Note that if building the jars with a version other than 2.13.x, you need to set the `SCALA_VERSION` variable or change it in `bin/kafka-run-class.sh` to run the quick start.*\n119: \n120: You can pass either the major version (eg 2.12) or the full version (eg 2.12.7):\n121: \n122:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\n123:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 test\n124:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 releaseTarGz\n125: \n126: ### Running a task with all the scala versions enabled by default you can run all the tests:\n141: \n142:     ./gradlew :streams:testAll\n143: \n144: ### Listing all gradle tasks ###\n145:     ./gradlew tasks\n146: \n147: ### Building IDE project ####\n148: *Note that this is not strictly necessary (IntelliJ IDEA has good built-in support for Gradle projects, for example).*\n149: \n150:     ./gradlew eclipse\n151:     ./gradlew idea\n152: \n153: The `eclipse` task has been configured to use `${project_dir}/build_eclipse` as Eclipse's build directory. Eclipse's default\n154: build directory (`${project_dir}/bin`) clashes with Kafka's scripts directory and we don't use Gradle's build directory\n155: to avoid known issues with this configuration.\n156: \n157: ### Publishing the jar for all versions of Scala and for all projects to maven ###\n158: The recommended command is:\n159: \n160:     ./gradlewAll publish\n161: \n162: For ### Building the test jar ###\n221:     ./gradlew testJar\n222: \n223: ### Running code quality checks ###\n224: There are two code quality analysis tools that we regularly run, spotbugs and checkstyle.\n225: \n226: #### Checkstyle ####\n227: Checkstyle enforces a consistent coding style in Kafka.\n228: You can run checkstyle using:\n229: \n230:     ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest They are also printed to the console. The build will fail if Checkstyle fails.\n234: \n235: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessCheck` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\n236: \n237: #### Spotless ####\n238: The import order is a part of static check. please call `spotlessApply` (require JDK 11+) to optimize the imports of Java codes before filing pull request.\n239: \n240:     ./gradlew spotlessApply\n241: \n242: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessApply` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\n243: \n244: #### Spotbugs ####\n245: Spotbugs uses static analysis to look for bugs in the code.\n246: You can run spotbugs using:\n247: \n248:     ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\n249: \n250: The spotbugs warnings will be found in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `reports/spotbugs/test.html` files in the subproject build\n251: directories. Defaults to the number of processors available to the JVM.\n280: * `maxScalacThreads`: maximum number of worker threads for the scalac backend. Defaults to the lowest of `8` and the number of processors\n281: available to the JVM. The value must be between 1 and 16 (inclusive). \n282: * `ignoreFailures`: ignore test failures from junit\n283: * `showStandardStreams`: shows standard out and standard error of the test JVM(s) on the console.\n284: * `skipSigning`: skips signing of artifacts.\n285: * `testLoggingEvents`: unit test events to be logged, separated by comma. For example `./gradlew -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed test`.\n286: * `xmlSpotBugsReport`: enable XML reports for spotBugs. This also disables HTML reports as only one can be enabled at a time.\n287: * `maxTestRetries`: maximum number of retries for a failing test case.\n288: * `maxTestRetryFailures`: maximum number of test failures before retrying is disabled for subsequent tests.\n289: * `enableTestCoverage`: enables test coverage plugins and tasks, including bytecode enhancement of classes required to track said\n290: coverage. Note that this introduces some overhead when running tests and hence why it's disabled by default (the overhead\n291: varies, but 15-20% is a reasonable estimate).\n292: * `keepAliveMode`: configures the keep alive mode for the Gradle compilation daemon - reuse improves start-up time. The values should \n293: be one of `daemon` or `session` (the default is `daemon`). `daemon` keeps the daemon alive until it's explicitly stopped while\n294: `session` keeps it alive until the end of the build session. This currently only affects the Scala compiler, see\n295: https://github.com/gradle/gradle/pull/21034 for a PR that attempts to do the same for the Java compiler.\n296: * `scalaOptimizerMode`: configures the optimizing behavior of the scala compiler, the value should be one of `none`, `method`, `inline-kafka` or\n297: `inline-scala` (the default is `inline-kafka`). `none` is the scala compiler default, which only eliminates unreachable code. `method` also\n298: includes method-local optimizations. `inline-kafka` adds inlining of methods within the kafka packages. Finally, `inline-scala` also\n299: includes inlining of methods within the scala library (which avoids lambda allocations for methods like `Option.exists`). `inline-scala` is\n300: only safe if the Scala library version is the same at compile time and runtime. Since we cannot guarantee this for all cases (for example, users\n301: may depend on the kafka jar for integration tests where they may include a scala library with a different version), we don't enable it by\n302: default. See https://www.lightbend.com/blog/scala-inliner-optimizer for more details.\n303: \n304: ### Running system tests ###\n305: \n306: See [tests/README.md](tests/README.md).\n307: \n308: ### Running in Vagrant ###\n309: \n310: See [vagrant/README.md](vagrant/README.md).\n311: \n312: ### Contribution ###\n313: \n314: Apache Kafka is interested in building the community; we would welcome any thoughts or [patches](https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA). This document covers the developer workflow, build system, testing infrastructure, and code review process.\n\n## 1. Build Prerequisites\n\n### Java Version Requirements\nKafka is built and tested with **Java 8, 11, 17, and 21**.\n\nKey points:\n- **Minimum Java version**: Java 8\n- **Release parameter**: Set to `8` to ensure binaries are compatible with Java 8 or higher\n- **Deprecation notes**:\n  - Java 8 support has been deprecated since Kafka 3.0 (removal planned for 4.0)\n  - Java 11 support for broker and tools has been deprecated since Kafka 3.7 (removal planned for 4.0)\n  - See [KIP-750](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308223) and [KIP-1013](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=284789510) for details\n\n### Scala Support\n- **Default version**: Scala 2.13.14\n- **Supported versions**: Scala 2.12 and 2.13\n- **Deprecation**: Scala 2.12 support has been deprecated since Kafka 3.0 (removal planned for 4.0)\n- See [KIP-751](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308218) for details\n\n### System Dependencies\n- **Git**: For cloning the repository and version control\n- **Gradle**: Build system (Gradle wrapper included in repo)\n- **Maven**: Required for Kafka Streams quickstart archetype builds (version 3.x)\n\n### Optional Tools\n- **IDE Support**: IntelliJ IDEA, Eclipse (IDE projects can be generated with Gradle)\n- **JMH**: For running microbenchmarks (included in `jmh-benchmarks/` module)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Gradle Build System\n\n### Overview\nKafka uses **Gradle** as its primary build system. The project is organized as a multi-module Gradle project with approximately 40+ submodules.\n\n### Key Modules\nThe main modules are defined in `settings.gradle`:\n- `clients` - Java client libraries\n- `core` - Kafka broker implementation\n- `connect` - Kafka Connect framework and connectors\n- `streams` - Kafka Streams library (with sub-modules for examples, scala, utils)\n- `server`, `server-common` - Server-side code\n- `storage` - Tiered storage implementation\n- `tools` - Kafka command-line tools\n- `log4j-appender` - Log4j integration\n- `examples` - Example code\n\n### Important Files\n- `build.gradle` - Root build configuration\n- `gradle.properties` - Project properties (version, Scala version, JVM args)\n- `settings.gradle` - Module definitions and Gradle Enterprise configuration\n- `gradle/dependencies.gradle` - Dependency versions\n\n### Building the Project\n\n#### Full Build\n```bash\n./gradlew jar\n```\n\n#### Build Specific Module\n```bash\n./gradlew core:jar\n./gradlew clients:jar\n./gradlew streams:testAll\n```\n\n#### Source JAR\n```bash\n./gradlew srcJar\n```\n\n#### Documentation\n```bash\n./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc    # Aggregated javadoc\n./gradlew javadoc              # Javadoc and scaladoc\n./gradlew javadocJar           # Javadoc jar for each module\n./gradlew scaladoc             # Scala documentation\n./gradlew scaladocJar          # Scaladoc jar for each module\n./gradlew docsJar              # Both javadoc and scaladoc jars\n```\n\n#### Building with Different Scala Versions\n```bash\n# Use Scala 2.12 for a specific task\n./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\n\n# Build with all supported Scala versions\n./gradlewAll jar\n./gradlewAll test\n./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\n```\n\n#### Release Artifacts\n```bash\n./gradlew clean releaseTarGz   # Creates gzipped tarball in core/build/distributions/\n```\n\n#### Rebuild Generated Messages\nWhen switching branches, RPC messages may need to be regenerated:\n```bash\n./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\n```\n\n### Gradle Properties and Options\n\nCommon properties (use with `-P` flag):\n- `scalaVersion` - Scala version (2.12 or 2.13)\n- `maxParallelForks` - Parallel test processes (default: number of processors)\n- `maxScalacThreads` - Scala compiler threads (default: min(8, processors), range: 1-16)\n- `ignoreFailures` - Ignore test failures (boolean)\n- `showStandardStreams` - Show stdout/stderr in tests (boolean)\n- `skipSigning` - Skip artifact signing (boolean)\n- `testLoggingEvents` - Comma-separated test events to log (started, passed, skipped, failed)\n- `xmlSpotBugsReport` - Enable XML reports for spotBugs (boolean)\n- `maxTestRetries` - Max retries for failing tests (default: 0)\n- `maxTestRetryFailures` - Max failures before disabling retries (default: 0)\n- `enableTestCoverage` - Enable test coverage (boolean, adds 15-20% overhead)\n- `keepAliveMode` - Gradle daemon keep-alive mode (daemon|session, default: daemon)\n- `scalaOptimizerMode` - Scala compiler optimization (none|method|inline-kafka|inline-scala, default: inline-kafka)\n\nExample:\n```bash\n./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=4 -PskipSigning=true test\n```\n\n### Listing Available Tasks\n```bash\n./gradlew tasks\n```\n\n### Building IDE Projects\n```bash\n./gradlew eclipse\n./gradlew idea\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\n### Test Framework\nKafka uses **JUnit 5 (Jupiter)** as its primary test framework. Custom test extensions are available for running integration tests with Kafka clusters.\n\n### Test Categories\n- **Unit Tests**: Fast, no cluster setup required\n- **Integration Tests**: Require cluster setup, tagged with `@Tag(\"integration\")`\n- **System Tests**: Complex multi-machine tests (see `tests/README.md`)\n\n### Running All Tests\n```bash\n./gradlew test                    # Unit + integration tests\n./gradlew unitTest                # Unit tests only\n./gradlew integrationTest         # Integration tests only\n```\n\n### Running Tests for Specific Module\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test            # All tests in clients module\n./gradlew core:test               # All tests in core module\n./gradlew streams:testAll         # All Streams tests\n```\n\n### Running Specific Test Class\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\n./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest\n```\n\n### Running Specific Test Method\n```bash\n./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\n./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\n```\n\n### Forcing Test Re-run Without Code Changes\n```bash\n./gradlew test --rerun\n./gradlew unitTest --rerun\n./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\n```\n\n### Repeatedly Running a Test (Useful for Flaky Tests)\n```bash\nI=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \"Completed run: $I\"; sleep 1; done\n```\n\n### Adjusting Test Logging\nBy default, limited logs are shown during tests. To increase verbosity:\n1. Modify `log4j.properties` in the module's `src/test/resources` directory\n2. Change log level from `WARN` to `INFO`:\n   ```properties\n   log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO\n   ```\n3. Run tests and check results in `{module}/build/test-results/test`\n\nExample:\n```bash\n./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest\n```\n\n### Test Retries\nBy default: each failed test retries once up to 5 retries per test run. Adjust:\n```bash\n./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\n```\n\nSee [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\n\n### Test Coverage Reports\n```bash\n# Whole project\n./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n\n# Single module\n./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n```\n\n### Custom Cluster Test Annotations\nFor integration tests requiring a running Kafka cluster:\n```java\n@ExtendWith(value = Array(classOf[ClusterTestExtensions]))\nclass ApiVersionsRequestTest {\n  @ClusterTest\n  def testBasic(clusterInstance: ClusterInstance): Unit = {\n    // Test code\n  }\n}\n```\n\nSee `core/src/test/java/kafka/test/junit/README.md` for full documentation.\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\n### CI Systems\nKafka uses **two CI systems**:\n\n1. **Jenkins** (Primary for development/PR builds)\n   - Defined in `Jenkinsfile` at repository root\n   - Runs on multiple Java/Scala version combinations\n   - Email notifications to `dev@kafka.apache.org` for failures\n\n2. **GitHub Actions** (Docker and promotion workflows)\n   - Located in `.github/workflows/`\n   - Used for Docker image building, testing, and promotion\n   - CVE scanning workflows\n\n### Jenkinsfile Overview\nThe `Jenkinsfile` defines a multi-stage pipeline:\n\n#### Build Stages (Parallel)\n1. **JDK 8 and Scala 2.12**\n   - Java: JDK 1.8 latest\n   - Scala: 2.12\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests, Streams archetype test\n\n2. **JDK 11 and Scala 2.13**\n   - Java: JDK 11 latest\n   - Scala: 2.13\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests (only on PRs)\n\n3. **JDK 17 and Scala 2.13**\n   - Java: JDK 17 latest\n   - Scala: 2.13\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests (only on PRs)\n\n4. **JDK 21 and Scala 2.13**\n   - Java: JDK 21 latest\n   - Scala: 2.13\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests\n\n#### CI Checks Run on Every Build\n1. **Validation** (code quality):\n   ```bash\n   ./retry_zinc ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=$SCALA_VERSION clean check -x test \\\n       --profile --continue -PxmlSpotBugsReport=true -PkeepAliveMode=\"session\"\n   ```\n   - Checkstyle (coding standards)\n   - Spotbugs (static analysis for bugs)\n   - Spotless (code formatting)\n   - Apache Rat (license headers)\n\n2. **Unit and Integration Tests**:\n   ```bash\n   ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=$SCALA_VERSION test \\\n       --profile --continue -PkeepAliveMode=\"session\" -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed \\\n       -PignoreFailures=true -PmaxParallelForks=2 -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=10\n   ```\n\n3. **Kafka Streams Archetype Test** (JDK 8 and JDK 21 only):\n   - Tests that Streams quickstart archetype compiles and works\n   - Uses Maven for archetype generation and compilation\n\n#### GitHub Actions Workflows\nLocated in `.github/workflows/`:\n- `docker_build_and_test.yml` - Build and test Docker images\n- `docker_official_image_build_and_test.yml` - Official Docker image workflow\n- `docker_promote.yml` - Promote RC Docker images to release\n- `docker_rc_release.yml` - Release candidate Docker image creation\n- `docker_scan.yml` - Nightly CVE scanning for Docker images\n- `stale.yml` - Manage stale issues/PRs\n\n### Pull Request Builds\n- Only triggered on PRs (when `CHANGE_ID` environment variable is set)\n- All four Java/Scala combinations run in parallel\n- Test results reported back to GitHub\n- Concurrent builds are aborted when new commits pushed\n\n### CI Environment Variables\n- `SCALA_VERSION` - Set for each build (2.12 or 2.13)\n- `CHANGE_ID` - Set by Jenkins for pull requests\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Before Creating a Pull Request\n\n**Important**: Review the official contribution guidelines first:\n- Apache Kafka Contributing Guide: https://kafka.apache.org/contributing.html\n- Contributing Code Changes: https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/Contributing+Code+Changes\n\n### JIRA Ticket Workflow\n\n1. **Browse Issues**:\n   - Visit https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n   - Look for unassigned issues with `newbie` label (good for first-time contributors)\n\n2. **Claim a Ticket**:\n   - Comment on the JIRA issue expressing interest\n   - Coordinate with committers and other contributors\n   - Fork the Apache Kafka repository\n\n3. **Branch Naming**:\n   - Not strictly enforced, but recommended: `KAFKA-XXXXX` (JIRA ticket number)\n   - Example: `KAFKA-12345-bug-fix-description`\n\n### Development Workflow\n\n1. **Setup**:\n   ```bash\n   # Clone your fork\n   git clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/kafka.git\n   cd kafka\n\n   # Add upstream remote\n   git remote add upstream https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\n\n   # Create feature branch\n   git checkout -b KAFKA-12345-description\n   ```\n\n2. **Code Changes**:\n   - Write code following Kafka's style guidelines\n   - Add/modify tests as appropriate\n   - Run code quality checks\n\n3. **Code Quality Checks**:\n   ```bash\n   # Checkstyle (enforces consistent coding style)\n   ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\n\n   # Spotbugs (static bug analysis)\n   ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\n\n   # Spotless (auto-format imports)\n   ./gradlew spotlessApply\n\n   # Note: Use JDK 11 or 17 for spotlessCheck and spotlessApply\n   # (Java 21 currently has issues - see README.md)\n   ```\n\n4. **Running Tests**:\n   ```bash\n   # Run all tests\n   ./gradlew test\n\n   # Run tests for changed modules\n   ./gradlew clients:test core:test\n\n   # Run specific test\n   ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest\n   ```\n\n5. **Commit**:\n   ```bash\n   # Write meaningful commit messages\n   # Format: [KAFKA-XXXXX] Brief description\n   #\n   # More detailed explanation of changes\n   git commit -am \"[KAFKA-12345] Fix bug in ProducerTest\"\n   ```\n\n6. **Push to Your Fork**:\n   ```bash\n   git push origin KAFKA-12345-description\n   ```\n\n7. **Create Pull Request**:\n   - Go to GitHub and create PR from your fork to `apache/kafka:main`\n   - PR title should reference JIRA ticket: `[KAFKA-12345] Brief description`\n   - Use the PR template provided in `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n   - Include:\n     - Summary of changes\n     - Testing strategy (unit/integration/system tests)\n     - Any documentation changes needed\n\n### Pull Request Template\n\nSee `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` in repository root. Include:\n\n```markdown\n*More detailed description of your change, if necessary.\nThe PR title and PR message become the squashed commit message.*\n\n*Summary of testing strategy (including rationale) for the feature or bug fix.\nUnit and/or integration tests are expected for any behaviour change and\nsystem tests should be considered for larger changes.*\n\n### Committer Checklist (excluded from commit message)\n- [ ] Verify design and implementation\n- [ ] Verify test coverage and CI build status\n- [ ] Verify documentation (including upgrade notes)\n```\n\n### Code Review Expectations\n\n1. **Reviewers**:\n   - Committers and experienced contributors review PRs\n   - Assign specific reviewers if known\n   - Multiple approvals typically required for major changes\n\n2. **Approval Process**:\n   - At least one +1 (approval) required\n   - CI build must pass (all 4 Java/Scala combinations)\n   - May request changes with specific feedback\n   - Committer can merge when approved\n\n3. **Code Standards**:\n   - Follow Kafka's checkstyle rules\n   - No spotbugs warnings\n   - Proper test coverage required\n   - Javadoc for public APIs\n   - Backward compatibility considerations\n\n4. **License Agreement**:\n   - By submitting a PR, you agree to license your contribution under the project's open source license (Apache License 2.0)\n   - This applies to all copyrighted material submitted via PR, email, or other means\n\n### After Approval\n\n1. **Final Updates**:\n   - Address any requested changes\n   - Push additional commits\n   - Ensure CI passes with updated code\n\n2. **Merge**:\n   - Committer merges the PR\n   - Commit message typically uses squashed format from PR template\n   - Closed PR automatically closes associated JIRA ticket\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Complete Step-by-Step Example\n\nScenario: Fix a bug in Kafka's producer where it incorrectly handles metadata refresh.\n\n#### Step 1: Find and Understand the Issue\n```bash\n# Browse JIRA at https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n# Find issue: KAFKA-14850 \"Producer not refreshing metadata on broker errors\"\n\n# Comment on the ticket:\n# \"I'd like to work on this bug. I'll investigate and submit a fix.\"\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Setup Local Repository\n```bash\n# Fork apache/kafka on GitHub\n# Clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/kafka.git\ncd kafka\n\n# Add upstream remote\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\ngit fetch upstream\n\n# Create feature branch from main\ngit checkout -b KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Investigate and Code\n```bash\n# Explore relevant code\n# Look at clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/\n\n# Run existing tests to understand failure\n./gradlew clients:test --tests KafkaProducerTest\n\n# Identify the bug and write fix\n# Example: Update MetadataUpdater.java to refresh on broker errors\n\n# Write or update test\n# Example: Add test case to KafkaProducerTest\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Local Testing\n```bash\n# Run specific test to verify fix\n./gradlew clients:test --tests KafkaProducerTest.testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError\n\n# Run all client tests\n./gradlew clients:test\n\n# Run code quality checks\n./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessApply\n./gradlew spotbugsMain -x test\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Commit Changes\n```bash\n# Stage changes\ngit add -A\n\n# Commit with meaningful message\ngit commit -m \"[KAFKA-14850] Fix producer metadata not refreshing on broker errors\n\nWhen a producer encounters a broker error, it should refresh metadata\nimmediately rather than waiting for the next scheduled refresh.\n\nThis change updates MetadataUpdater to call maybeUpdate() when broker\nerrors are encountered, ensuring rapid recovery from broker failures.\n\nTesting:\n- Added unit test: testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError\n- Ran full client test suite: all tests pass\n- Code quality: checkstyle and spotbugs clean\"\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Push and Create PR\n```bash\n# Push to your fork\ngit push origin KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n\n# Go to GitHub and create Pull Request\n# - From: YOUR_USERNAME:KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n# - To: apache:kafka:main\n# - Title: [KAFKA-14850] Fix producer metadata not refreshing on broker errors\n# - Description:\n```\n\n#### Step 7: PR Description Template\n```markdown\n## Summary\nThe Kafka producer was not refreshing metadata when encountering broker errors,\nleading to extended periods of unavailability after broker restarts. This fix\nensures metadata is refreshed immediately upon broker errors.\n\n## Testing\n- Added unit test: `testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError()` in KafkaProducerTest\n- Verified: all 127 client tests pass\n- Code quality: checkstyle ✓, spotbugs ✓\n- No backward compatibility issues\n\n## Verification\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test\n```\n\nAll tests pass with 4 Java/Scala combinations on CI.\n```\n\n#### Step 8: Address Review Comments\n```bash\n# If reviewers request changes:\n# Make edits to the code\nvim clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java\n\n# Run tests again\n./gradlew clients:test --tests KafkaProducerTest.testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError\n\n# Commit the changes\ngit add -A\ngit commit -m \"[KAFKA-14850] Address review comments: improve error handling\"\n\n# Push updated commit\ngit push origin KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Merge\n```bash\n# Once approved by committer, PR is merged\n# You'll see the commit in main branch:\ngit fetch upstream\ngit log upstream/main | grep KAFKA-14850\n```\n\n#### Step 10: Cleanup\n```bash\n# Delete your local branch\ngit checkout main\ngit branch -D KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n\n# Delete remote branch\ngit push origin --delete KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n\n# Update local main\ngit pull upstream main\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Official Documentation\n- **Apache Kafka Website**: https://kafka.apache.org\n- **Contributing Guide**: https://kafka.apache.org/contributing.html\n- **Contributing Code Changes**: https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/Contributing+Code+Changes\n- **Protocol Guide**: https://kafka.apache.org/protocol.html\n- **Quickstart**: https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\n\n### Key Documentation Files in Repo\n- `README.md` - This document covers the developer workflow, build system, testing infrastructure, and code review process.\n\n## 1. Build Prerequisites\n\n### Java Version Requirements\nKafka is built and tested with **Java 8, 11, 17, and 21**.\n\nKey points:\n- **Minimum Java version**: Java 8\n- **Release parameter**: Set to `8` to ensure binaries are compatible with Java 8 or higher\n- **Deprecation notes**:\n  - Java 8 support has been deprecated since Kafka 3.0 (removal planned for 4.0)\n  - Java 11 support for broker and tools has been deprecated since Kafka 3.7 (removal planned for 4.0)\n  - See [KIP-750](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308223) and [KIP-1013](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=284789510) for details\n\n### Scala Support\n- **Default version**: Scala 2.13.14\n- **Supported versions**: Scala 2.12 and 2.13\n- **Deprecation**: Scala 2.12 support has been deprecated since Kafka 3.0 (removal planned for 4.0)\n- See [KIP-751](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308218) for details\n\n### System Dependencies\n- **Git**: For cloning the repository and version control\n- **Gradle**: Build system (Gradle wrapper included in repo)\n- **Maven**: Required for Kafka Streams quickstart archetype builds (version 3.x)\n\n### Optional Tools\n- **IDE Support**: IntelliJ IDEA, Eclipse (IDE projects can be generated with Gradle)\n- **JMH**: For running microbenchmarks (included in `jmh-benchmarks/` module)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Gradle Build System\n\n### Overview\nKafka uses **Gradle** as its primary build system. The project is organized as a multi-module Gradle project with approximately 40+ submodules.\n\n### Key Modules\nThe main modules are defined in `settings.gradle`:\n- `clients` - Java client libraries\n- `core` - Kafka broker implementation\n- `connect` - Kafka Connect framework and connectors\n- `streams` - Kafka Streams library (with sub-modules for examples, scala, utils)\n- `server`, `server-common` - Server-side code\n- `storage` - Tiered storage implementation\n- `tools` - Kafka command-line tools\n- `log4j-appender` - Log4j integration\n- `examples` - Example code\n\n### Important Files\n- `build.gradle` - Root build configuration\n- `gradle.properties` - Project properties (version, Scala version, JVM args)\n- `settings.gradle` - Module definitions and Gradle Enterprise configuration\n- `gradle/dependencies.gradle` - Dependency versions\n\n### Building the Project\n\n#### Full Build\n```bash\n./gradlew jar\n```\n\n#### Build Specific Module\n```bash\n./gradlew core:jar\n./gradlew clients:jar\n./gradlew streams:testAll\n```\n\n#### Source JAR\n```bash\n./gradlew srcJar\n```\n\n#### Documentation\n```bash\n./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc    # Aggregated javadoc\n./gradlew javadoc              # Javadoc and scaladoc\n./gradlew javadocJar           # Javadoc jar for each module\n./gradlew scaladoc             # Scala documentation\n./gradlew scaladocJar          # Scaladoc jar for each module\n./gradlew docsJar              # Both javadoc and scaladoc jars\n```\n\n#### Building with Different Scala Versions\n```bash\n# Use Scala 2.12 for a specific task\n./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\n\n# Build with all supported Scala versions\n./gradlewAll jar\n./gradlewAll test\n./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\n```\n\n#### Release Artifacts\n```bash\n./gradlew clean releaseTarGz   # Creates gzipped tarball in core/build/distributions/\n```\n\n#### Rebuild Generated Messages\nWhen switching branches, RPC messages may need to be regenerated:\n```bash\n./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\n```\n\n### Gradle Properties and Options\n\nCommon properties (use with `-P` flag):\n- `scalaVersion` - Scala version (2.12 or 2.13)\n- `maxParallelForks` - Parallel test processes (default: number of processors)\n- `maxScalacThreads` - Scala compiler threads (default: min(8, processors), range: 1-16)\n- `ignoreFailures` - Ignore test failures (boolean)\n- `showStandardStreams` - Show stdout/stderr in tests (boolean)\n- `skipSigning` - Skip artifact signing (boolean)\n- `testLoggingEvents` - Comma-separated test events to log (started, passed, skipped, failed)\n- `xmlSpotBugsReport` - Enable XML reports for spotBugs (boolean)\n- `maxTestRetries` - Max retries for failing tests (default: 0)\n- `maxTestRetryFailures` - Max failures before disabling retries (default: 0)\n- `enableTestCoverage` - Enable test coverage (boolean, adds 15-20% overhead)\n- `keepAliveMode` - Gradle daemon keep-alive mode (daemon|session, default: daemon)\n- `scalaOptimizerMode` - Scala compiler optimization (none|method|inline-kafka|inline-scala, default: inline-kafka)\n\nExample:\n```bash\n./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=4 -PskipSigning=true test\n```\n\n### Listing Available Tasks\n```bash\n./gradlew tasks\n```\n\n### Building IDE Projects\n```bash\n./gradlew eclipse\n./gradlew idea\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\n### Test Framework\nKafka uses **JUnit 5 (Jupiter)** as its primary test framework. Custom test extensions are available for running integration tests with Kafka clusters.\n\n### Test Categories\n- **Unit Tests**: Fast, no cluster setup required\n- **Integration Tests**: Require cluster setup, tagged with `@Tag(\"integration\")`\n- **System Tests**: Complex multi-machine tests (see `tests/README.md`)\n\n### Running All Tests\n```bash\n./gradlew test                    # Unit + integration tests\n./gradlew unitTest                # Unit tests only\n./gradlew integrationTest         # Integration tests only\n```\n\n### Running Tests for Specific Module\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test            # All tests in clients module\n./gradlew core:test               # All tests in core module\n./gradlew streams:testAll         # All Streams tests\n```\n\n### Running Specific Test Class\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\n./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest\n```\n\n### Running Specific Test Method\n```bash\n./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\n./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\n```\n\n### Forcing Test Re-run Without Code Changes\n```bash\n./gradlew test --rerun\n./gradlew unitTest --rerun\n./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\n```\n\n### Repeatedly Running a Test (Useful for Flaky Tests)\n```bash\nI=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \"Completed run: $I\"; sleep 1; done\n```\n\n### Adjusting Test Logging\nBy default, limited logs are shown during tests. To increase verbosity:\n1. Modify `log4j.properties` in the module's `src/test/resources` directory\n2. Change log level from `WARN` to `INFO`:\n   ```properties\n   log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO\n   ```\n3. Run tests and check results in `{module}/build/test-results/test`\n\nExample:\n```bash\n./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest\n```\n\n### Test Retries\nBy default: each failed test retries once up to 5 retries per test run. Adjust:\n```bash\n./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\n```\n\nSee [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\n\n### Test Coverage Reports\n```bash\n# Whole project\n./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n\n# Single module\n./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n```\n\n### Custom Cluster Test Annotations\nFor integration tests requiring a running Kafka cluster:\n```java\n@ExtendWith(value = Array(classOf[ClusterTestExtensions]))\nclass ApiVersionsRequestTest {\n  @ClusterTest\n  def testBasic(clusterInstance: ClusterInstance): Unit = {\n    // Test code\n  }\n}\n```\n\nSee `core/src/test/java/kafka/test/junit/README.md` for full documentation.\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\n### CI Systems\nKafka uses **two CI systems**:\n\n1. **Jenkins** (Primary for development/PR builds)\n   - Defined in `Jenkinsfile` at repository root\n   - Runs on multiple Java/Scala version combinations\n   - Email notifications to `dev@kafka.apache.org` for failures\n\n2. **GitHub Actions** (Docker and promotion workflows)\n   - Located in `.github/workflows/`\n   - Used for Docker image building, testing, and promotion\n   - CVE scanning workflows\n\n### Jenkinsfile Overview\nThe `Jenkinsfile` defines a multi-stage pipeline:\n\n#### Build Stages (Parallel)\n1. **JDK 8 and Scala 2.12**\n   - Java: JDK 1.8 latest\n   - Scala: 2.12\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests, Streams archetype test\n\n2. **JDK 11 and Scala 2.13**\n   - Java: JDK 11 latest\n   - Scala: 2.13\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests (only on PRs)\n\n3. **JDK 17 and Scala 2.13**\n   - Java: JDK 17 latest\n   - Scala: 2.13\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests (only on PRs)\n\n4. **JDK 21 and Scala 2.13**\n   - Java: JDK 21 latest\n   - Scala: 2.13\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n   - Runs: validation, tests\n\n#### CI Checks Run on Every Build\n1. **Validation** (code quality):\n   ```bash\n   ./retry_zinc ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=$SCALA_VERSION clean check -x test \\\n       --profile --continue -PxmlSpotBugsReport=true -PkeepAliveMode=\"session\"\n   ```\n   - Checkstyle (coding standards)\n   - Spotbugs (static analysis for bugs)\n   - Spotless (code formatting)\n   - Apache Rat (license headers)\n\n2. **Unit and Integration Tests**:\n   ```bash\n   ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=$SCALA_VERSION test \\\n       --profile --continue -PkeepAliveMode=\"session\" -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed \\\n       -PignoreFailures=true -PmaxParallelForks=2 -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=10\n   ```\n\n3. **Kafka Streams Archetype Test** (JDK 8 and JDK 21 only):\n   - Tests that Streams quickstart archetype compiles and works\n   - Uses Maven for archetype generation and compilation\n\n#### GitHub Actions Workflows\nLocated in `.github/workflows/`:\n- `docker_build_and_test.yml` - Build and test Docker images\n- `docker_official_image_build_and_test.yml` - Official Docker image workflow\n- `docker_promote.yml` - Promote RC Docker images to release\n- `docker_rc_release.yml` - Release candidate Docker image creation\n- `docker_scan.yml` - Nightly CVE scanning for Docker images\n- `stale.yml` - Manage stale issues/PRs\n\n### Pull Request Builds\n- Only triggered on PRs (when `CHANGE_ID` environment variable is set)\n- All four Java/Scala combinations run in parallel\n- Test results reported back to GitHub\n- Concurrent builds are aborted when new commits pushed\n\n### CI Environment Variables\n- `SCALA_VERSION` - Set for each build (2.12 or 2.13)\n- `CHANGE_ID` - Set by Jenkins for pull requests\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Before Creating a Pull Request\n\n**Important**: Review the official contribution guidelines first:\n- Apache Kafka Contributing Guide: https://kafka.apache.org/contributing.html\n- Contributing Code Changes: https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/Contributing+Code+Changes\n\n### JIRA Ticket Workflow\n\n1. **Browse Issues**:\n   - Visit https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n   - Look for unassigned issues with `newbie` label (good for first-time contributors)\n\n2. **Claim a Ticket**:\n   - Comment on the JIRA issue expressing interest\n   - Coordinate with committers and other contributors\n   - Fork the Apache Kafka repository\n\n3. **Branch Naming**:\n   - Not strictly enforced, but recommended: `KAFKA-XXXXX` (JIRA ticket number)\n   - Example: `KAFKA-12345-bug-fix-description`\n\n### Development Workflow\n\n1. **Setup**:\n   ```bash\n   # Clone your fork\n   git clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/kafka.git\n   cd kafka\n\n   # Add upstream remote\n   git remote add upstream https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\n\n   # Create feature branch\n   git checkout -b KAFKA-12345-description\n   ```\n\n2. **Code Changes**:\n   - Write code following Kafka's style guidelines\n   - Add/modify tests as appropriate\n   - Run code quality checks\n\n3. **Code Quality Checks**:\n   ```bash\n   # Checkstyle (enforces consistent coding style)\n   ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\n\n   # Spotbugs (static bug analysis)\n   ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\n\n   # Spotless (auto-format imports)\n   ./gradlew spotlessApply\n\n   # Note: Use JDK 11 or 17 for spotlessCheck and spotlessApply\n   # (Java 21 currently has issues - see README.md)\n   ```\n\n4. **Running Tests**:\n   ```bash\n   # Run all tests\n   ./gradlew test\n\n   # Run tests for changed modules\n   ./gradlew clients:test core:test\n\n   # Run specific test\n   ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest\n   ```\n\n5. **Commit**:\n   ```bash\n   # Write meaningful commit messages\n   # Format: [KAFKA-XXXXX] Brief description\n   #\n   # More detailed explanation of changes\n   git commit -am \"[KAFKA-12345] Fix bug in ProducerTest\"\n   ```\n\n6. **Push to Your Fork**:\n   ```bash\n   git push origin KAFKA-12345-description\n   ```\n\n7. **Create Pull Request**:\n   - Go to GitHub and create PR from your fork to `apache/kafka:main`\n   - PR title should reference JIRA ticket: `[KAFKA-12345] Brief description`\n   - Use the PR template provided in `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n   - Include:\n     - Summary of changes\n     - Testing strategy (unit/integration/system tests)\n     - Any documentation changes needed\n\n### Pull Request Template\n\nSee `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` in repository root. Include:\n\n```markdown\n*More detailed description of your change, if necessary.\nThe PR title and PR message become the squashed commit message.*\n\n*Summary of testing strategy (including rationale) for the feature or bug fix.\nUnit and/or integration tests are expected for any behaviour change and\nsystem tests should be considered for larger changes.*\n\n### Committer Checklist (excluded from commit message)\n- [ ] Verify design and implementation\n- [ ] Verify test coverage and CI build status\n- [ ] Verify documentation (including upgrade notes)\n```\n\n### Code Review Expectations\n\n1. **Reviewers**:\n   - Committers and experienced contributors review PRs\n   - Assign specific reviewers if known\n   - Multiple approvals typically required for major changes\n\n2. **Approval Process**:\n   - At least one +1 (approval) required\n   - CI build must pass (all 4 Java/Scala combinations)\n   - May request changes with specific feedback\n   - Committer can merge when approved\n\n3. **Code Standards**:\n   - Follow Kafka's checkstyle rules\n   - No spotbugs warnings\n   - Proper test coverage required\n   - Javadoc for public APIs\n   - Backward compatibility considerations\n\n4. **License Agreement**:\n   - By submitting a PR, you agree to license your contribution under the project's open source license (Apache License 2.0)\n   - This applies to all copyrighted material submitted via PR, email, or other means\n\n### After Approval\n\n1. **Final Updates**:\n   - Address any requested changes\n   - Push additional commits\n   - Ensure CI passes with updated code\n\n2. **Merge**:\n   - Committer merges the PR\n   - Commit message typically uses squashed format from PR template\n   - Closed PR automatically closes associated JIRA ticket\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Complete Step-by-Step Example\n\nScenario: Fix a bug in Kafka's producer where it incorrectly handles metadata refresh.\n\n#### Step 1: Find and Understand the Issue\n```bash\n# Browse JIRA at https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n# Find issue: KAFKA-14850 \"Producer not refreshing metadata on broker errors\"\n\n# Comment on the ticket:\n# \"I'd like to work on this bug. I'll investigate and submit a fix.\"\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Setup Local Repository\n```bash\n# Fork apache/kafka on GitHub\n# Clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/kafka.git\ncd kafka\n\n# Add upstream remote\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\ngit fetch upstream\n\n# Create feature branch from main\ngit checkout -b KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Investigate and Code\n```bash\n# Explore relevant code\n# Look at clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/\n\n# Run existing tests to understand failure\n./gradlew clients:test --tests KafkaProducerTest\n\n# Identify the bug and write fix\n# Example: Update MetadataUpdater.java to refresh on broker errors\n\n# Write or update test\n# Example: Add test case to KafkaProducerTest\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Local Testing\n```bash\n# Run specific test to verify fix\n./gradlew clients:test --tests KafkaProducerTest.testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError\n\n# Run all client tests\n./gradlew clients:test\n\n# Run code quality checks\n./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessApply\n./gradlew spotbugsMain -x test\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Commit Changes\n```bash\n# Stage changes\ngit add -A\n\n# Commit with meaningful message\ngit commit -m \"[KAFKA-14850] Fix producer metadata not refreshing on broker errors\n\nWhen a producer encounters a broker error, it should refresh metadata\nimmediately rather than waiting for the next scheduled refresh.\n\nThis change updates MetadataUpdater to call maybeUpdate() when broker\nerrors are encountered, ensuring rapid recovery from broker failures.\n\nTesting:\n- Added unit test: testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError\n- Ran full client test suite: all tests pass\n- Code quality: checkstyle and spotbugs clean\"\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Push and Create PR\n```bash\n# Push to your fork\ngit push origin KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n\n# Go to GitHub and create Pull Request\n# - From: YOUR_USERNAME:KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n# - To: apache:kafka:main\n# - Title: [KAFKA-14850] Fix producer metadata not refreshing on broker errors\n# - Description:\n```\n\n#### Step 7: PR Description Template\n```markdown\n## Summary\nThe Kafka producer was not refreshing metadata when encountering broker errors,\nleading to extended periods of unavailability after broker restarts. This fix\nensures metadata is refreshed immediately upon broker errors.\n\n## Testing\n- Added unit test: `testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError()` in KafkaProducerTest\n- Verified: all 127 client tests pass\n- Code quality: checkstyle ✓, spotbugs ✓\n- No backward compatibility issues\n\n## Verification\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test\n```\n\nAll tests pass with 4 Java/Scala combinations on CI.\n```\n\n#### Step 8: Address Review Comments\n```bash\n# If reviewers request changes:\n# Make edits to the code\nvim clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java\n\n# Run tests again\n./gradlew clients:test --tests KafkaProducerTest.testMetadataRefreshOnBrokerError\n\n# Commit the changes\ngit add -A\ngit commit -m \"[KAFKA-14850] Address review comments: improve error handling\"\n\n# Push updated commit\ngit push origin KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Merge\n```bash\n# Once approved by committer, PR is merged\n# You'll see the commit in main branch:\ngit fetch upstream\ngit log upstream/main | grep KAFKA-14850\n```\n\n#### Step 10: Cleanup\n```bash\n# Delete your local branch\ngit checkout main\ngit branch -D KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n\n# Delete remote branch\ngit push origin --delete KAFKA-14850-producer-metadata-refresh\n\n# Update local main\ngit pull upstream main\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n### Official Documentation\n- **Apache Kafka Website**: https://kafka.apache.org\n- **Contributing Guide**: https://kafka.apache.org/contributing.html\n- **Contributing Code Changes**: https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA/Contributing+Code+Changes\n- **Protocol Guide**: https://kafka.apache.org/protocol.html\n- **Quickstart**: https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\n\n### Key Documentation Files in Repo\n- `README.md` - Build and test instructions\n- `tests/README.md` - System tests and Trogdor framework\n- `vagrant/README.md` - Vagrant development environment\n- `docker/README.md` - Docker build and testing\n- `jmh-benchmarks/README.md` - JMH microbenchmarks\n- `core/src/test/java/kafka/test/junit/README.md` - Cluster test annotations\n\n### JIRA\n- **Issue Tracking**: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n- Look for issues with `newbie` label for first-time contributions\n\n### Development Tools\n- **IDE Support**: IntelliJ IDEA has built-in Gradle support; can also generate with `./gradlew idea`\n- **Build Scans**: https://ge.apache.org (Apache Gradle Enterprise)\n- **Dependency Analysis**:\n  ```bash\n  ./gradlew allDeps\n  ./gradlew dependencyUpdates\n  ```\n\n### Common Issues and Solutions\n\n**Issue**: Tests fail with Java 21 related to spotless\n- **Solution**: Run spotlessCheck/spotlessApply with JDK 11 or 17 instead\n\n**Issue**: Long build times\n- **Solution**: Use `-PmaxParallelForks=1` to reduce parallelism if tests are flaky\n\n**Issue**: Stale lock files\n- **Solution**: Run `./gradlew clean` to reset build state\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kafka contribution workflow:\n\n1. **Find** an issue on JIRA (https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA)\n2. **Clone** your fork and create a feature branch\n3. **Code** your fix with tests\n4. **Verify** with `./gradlew test` and code quality checks\n5. **Commit** with meaningful message referencing JIRA ticket\n6. **Push** to your fork and create a PR\n7. **Respond** to review comments\n8. **Merge** when approved by committers\n\nThe Kafka project welcomes contributions from the community.
